 ease," *vide supra p. 25; Pupius p.’24o inquit: ,,It is
 impossible not to take notice that Homer niakes repeti-
 tion after repetition: Agamemnon speaks the same

 V Words as in the eleventh Odyssey: Amphimedon the

 same as in the second; and the whole account of
 the suitors destruction is no more than a recital of what
 the reader already knows. Was Homer tired at the end
 of his work , and Would not give himself the· labour of
 invention? I confess we may lose our appetite to see the

 ’ < same entertainment thus continually served up in the

 very same manner, wjthout so much as ·a new garnish-

 ‘ ment. I fear the words of Vlysses may sometimes be‘

 applicable to Homer;
